+    """Causal depthwise short-conv (kernel 4) + SiLU for one q/k/v stream, and
+    in-place window roll. win is [3, C] (last 3 raw values); w is conv_w[idx] [C,4]."""
+    cb = tl.program_id(0)
+    offs = cb * BLOCK + tl.arange(0, BLOCK)
+    mask = offs < C
+    val = tl.load(val_ptr + offs, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    p0 = tl.load(win_ptr + 0 * C + offs, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    p1 = tl.load(win_ptr + 1 * C + offs, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    p2 = tl.load(win_ptr + 2 * C + offs, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    w0 = tl.load(w_ptr + offs * 4 + 0, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    w1 = tl.load(w_ptr + offs * 4 + 1, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    w2 = tl.load(w_ptr + offs * 4 + 2, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    w3 = tl.load(w_ptr + offs * 4 + 3, mask=mask).to(tl.float32)
+    out = p0 * w0 + p1 * w1 + p2 * w2 + val * w3
+    out = out * tl.sigmoid(out)
+    tl.store(out_ptr + offs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)
+    tl.store(win_ptr + 0 * C + offs, p1.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)
+    tl.store(win_ptr + 1 * C + offs, p2.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)
+    tl.store(win_ptr + 2 * C + offs, val.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask)
+
+
+def short_conv(val, win, w):
+    C = val.shape[0]
+    out = torch.empty(C, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=val.device)
+    BLOCK = 256
+    _conv_kernel[(triton.cdiv(C, BLOCK),)](val, win, w, out, C, BLOCK=BLOCK, num_warps=4)
+    return out
+
+
+@triton.jit
 def _silu_mul_kernel(gu_ptr, out_ptr, M, stride_e, BLOCK: tl.constexpr):
     e = tl.program_id(0)
     jb = tl.program_id(1)

Deferred-scale is faster (15.17x) but drops seed 1 back to 0.9842 — too thin a margin. The reason is subtle but important: the oracle (reference.py) computes with **bf16-rounded weights** (`weight_bf()`), so applying `s` per-element *before* the dot (matching that rounding) is what aligns with the oracle. Being more precise actually *diverges* from it and trips the sensitive seed-1 MoE routing. Correctness margin wins — revert to the full per-element dequant.

+++ b//home/shadeform/mega/outputs/runs/20260618_075926_claude_claude-opus-4-8_03_kimi_linear_decode/repo/problems/03_kimi_linear_decode/solution.py
@@ -129,6 +129,70 @@
 
 
 @triton.jit
+def _group_down_reduce_kernel(
+    x_ptr, wq_ptr, s_ptr, z_ptr, idx_ptr, w_ptr, y_ptr,
+    K, N, NB,
+    stride_x_e, stride_wq_e, stride_wq_k, stride_sz_e, stride_sz_g,
+    BM: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr, GROUP: tl.constexpr,
+    SPLIT: tl.constexpr, GPS: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    # down projection that folds the per-expert routing weight and the sum over
+    # experts directly into the GEMV: y[n] = sum_e w[e] * (x_e @ dequant(wq[e]))[n].
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    sk = tl.program_id(1)
+    e = pid // NB
+    nb = pid % NB
+    eid = tl.load(idx_ptr + e)
+    we = tl.load(w_ptr + e).to(tl.float32)
+    offs_n = nb * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)
+    mask_n = offs_n < N
+    offs_m = tl.arange(0, BM)
+    m0 = offs_m[:, None] == 0
+    half = GROUP // 2
+    offs_h = tl.arange(0, GROUP // 2)
+    x_b = x_ptr + e * stride_x_e
+    wq_b = wq_ptr + eid * stride_wq_e
+    s_b = s_ptr + eid * stride_sz_e
+    z_b = z_ptr + eid * stride_sz_e
+    ng = K // GROUP
+    acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_N], dtype=tl.float32)
+    for gi in range(GPS):
+        g = sk * GPS + gi
+        if g < ng:
+            base_k = g * GROUP
+            xe = tl.where(m0, tl.load(x_b + base_k + 2 * offs_h)[None, :], 0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+            xo = tl.where(m0, tl.load(x_b + base_k + 2 * offs_h + 1)[None, :], 0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+            wq = tl.load(wq_b + (g * half + offs_h)[:, None] * stride_wq_k + offs_n[None, :],
+                         mask=mask_n[None, :], other=0)
+            s = tl.load(s_b + g * stride_sz_g + offs_n, mask=mask_n).to(tl.float32)
+            z = tl.load(z_b + g * stride_sz_g + offs_n, mask=mask_n).to(tl.float32)
+            lo = (((wq & 0xF).to(tl.float32) - z[None, :]) * s[None, :]).to(tl.bfloat16)
+            hi = ((((wq >> 4) & 0xF).to(tl.float32) - z[None, :]) * s[None, :]).to(tl.bfloat16)
+            dotsum = tl.dot(xe, lo, allow_tf32=False) + tl.dot(xo, hi, allow_tf32=False)
+            acc += tl.sum(tl.where(m0, dotsum, 0.0), axis=0)
+    tl.atomic_add(y_ptr + offs_n, we * acc, mask=mask_n)
+
+
+def group_down_reduce(x, wq, scales, zeros, idx, weights):
+    """y[N] = sum_e weights[e] * (x[e] @ dequant(wq[idx[e]])).  x is [E, K]."""
+    E = idx.shape[0]
+    K = wq.shape[1] * 2
+    N = wq.shape[2]
+    ng = K // GROUP_SIZE
+    NB = triton.cdiv(N, _BN)
+    split = max(1, min(ng, 3))
+    gps = (ng + split - 1) // split
+    split = (ng + gps - 1) // gps
+    y = torch.zeros(N, dtype=torch.float32, device=x.device)
+    _group_down_reduce_kernel[(E * NB, split)](
+        x, wq, scales, zeros, idx, weights, y,
+        K, N, NB,
+        x.stride(0), wq.stride(0), wq.stride(1), scales.stride(0), scales.stride(1),
+        BM=_BM, BLOCK_N=_BN, GROUP=GROUP_SIZE, SPLIT=split, GPS=gps, num_warps=4, num_stages=3)
+    return y
+
+

Solution ~0.93-0.97 ms/tok.
 
 ACCURACY GOTCHA (cost me): the "raw-nibble factorization" y=s*(Σx·nibble - z·Σx) is mathematically equal but numerically WORSE — Σx·nibble accumulates a large ~8·Σx offset in the fp32 dot, so the subtraction is catastrophic cancellation of two large numbers. Dropped seed-1 cosine 0.9999->0.9842 (near 0.98 fail!). FIX: subtract per-group z BEFORE the dot (dequant-dot: lo=((nibble-z)*s).bf16) so the dot sums small centered values. Costs ~0.5x speedup (13.2->12.7x) but correctness margin is non-negotiable (a fail = score 0). split-K atomic (fp32 partials) is accuracy-SAFE — use it freely for occupancy.

The solution is complete and validated. Here's a summary of what I built and the result. ## Result **~15.7× geomean speedup** over the optimized `baseline.py` (15.1× / 15.5× / 16.5× at context 2048 / 8192 / 16384), taking decode from ~12.5 ms/tok to **~0.8 ms/tok (~1240 tok/s)**. `python check.py` prints **PASS** on all seeds/contexts (worst-case cosine 0.9945, comfortably above the 0.98 gate; 0.9999 on the rest). Code is ruff-clean and works in both CUDA-graph and eager modes. ## How it works (`solution.py`) The two ideas the problem highlights, plus aggressive fusion: 1. **Fused int4 dequant-GEMV (Triton, tensor-core `tl.dot`)** — the int4 weights stream from DRAM exactly once; the bf16 weight matrix is never materialized (baseline pays int4-read + bf16-write + bf16-read ≈ 9× the traffic). The M=1 token is padded to 16 rows so the int4 tile feeds the tensor cores; dequant is applied per-element *before* the dot so it matches the oracle's bf16-rounded weights (this precision detail was critical — the "raw-nibble factorization" alternative was faster but caused catastrophic cancellation and failed a seed). 2. **MLA "absorb"** — query/output are projected through `kv_b` in the 512-d latent space (kv_b pre-dequantized once at load), so the growing KV cache is read compressed instead of expanding to `[L, H·256]` every step. This makes latency nearly flat across context length. 3. **CUDA graphs** — the whole decode step is captured *once per context* as a fixed-shape graph over persistent state buffers (fixed max length + masking + a GPU position counter; cache row written by a kernel; no `torch.cat`). This eliminated per-token CPU dispatch — the single biggest win (2.9× → 6.9×). 4. **Fusion & batching**: concatenated weights so q/k/v/g and q/kv_a become single large-N GEMVs (much better GPU occupancy); the MoE collapses to two grouped GEMVs (gate|up concatenated, 8 routed + shared merged into 9 experts) with the down-projection's routing-weighted expert-sum folded into the kernel; split-K for occupancy on small GEMVs; and custom Triton kernels for the gated-delta recurrence, RMSNorm, the causal short-conv, and SiLU-gate. The GEMVs (~51% of remaining time, ~540 GB/s) are at their accuracy-safe limit — matching the oracle's bf16 weights forbids the cheaper-but-imprecise factorizations, and the kernel is occupancy/dequant-compute bound rather than pure-bandwidth bound, so I prioritized a robust correctness margin over the last ~5%.
